<name>Meredith Smith< /name>< text>
Not sure what others are saying about things not seeming fresh but went there on a monday night and everything was perfect.

We got:
Shrimp dumplings
Scallion pancakes- so crisp, so many layers probably the best I've had
Seafood crispy noodles
Chinese broccoli with garlic sauce
Turnip cakes- we weren't sure what this was when we ordered it but it was soft in texture and fishy. We liked it a lot.
Green sesame balls- soft in texture, not greasy and a very strong but not overpowering sesame flavor.

Everything was very good. We spent a decent amount of money, but plenty of food for the two of us and enough leftovers for a couple lunches as well. We will definitely be back!</text>

< review>
We ate there today for lunch and I am rating it a 5 for a specific reason:  To celebrate that Davis finally has a real dim sum restaurant.   Dim sum isn't cheap, but that's okay, it's dim sum.   They may not have had absolutely every item that a dim sum veteran would expect, but that's okay, they still had dozens of choices and for us it was plenty.  They had duck, they had pork buns, they had Asian broccoli, they had shrimp rolls, they had chicken feet, they had lots of stuff.   Yay!

They also had plenty of customers, at least on Saturday for lunch.  I'm not sure why another review said that they don't do dim sum on weekends.   Maybe just opening month confusion?   I expect that they will fix most of their opening kinks, and I also hope so.   Regardless, my wife and I were sated and satisfied.<//review>

< review>
Was super excited to try this place as dim sum is one of our family favorites.

Off the bat, they do not serve dim sum on weekends. Not a deal breaker, but disappointing.

Second, the phone numbers listed do not work.

Third, when we finally got the chance to try their food, they were out of some items and do not make certain items at night. Again, not a deal breaker, but it is always disappointing when you can't get your favorites.

As this was our first time trying Well Season, we took a dim sum menu and regular menu and picked items that are favorites and a couple items we have not tried, just to see what was good. We spent $50 on enough food to feed three people. Overall, the experience was disappointing and the food was nothing special. Nothing was very hot, barely even warm, and to quote one of the others eating with me, "Nothing tastes like it was made today".

We ordered:

Green Onion Pancake: A family favorite, but this one was not crispy, had little to no green onion flavor, and was excessively oily.

Baked BBQ Pork Buns: Another staple, this is the one they said they do not make at night, but they made it for us anyways. The pork was good and tender, the bun was cooked perfectly. I would eat this again.

BBQ Pork Rice Noodle: Another favorite, but they were out of it. They recommended the House Special Pan Fried Pork Bun. It was reminiscent of a potsticker,  but the filling was bland and the bun tasted like it was cooked in a pan in which the oil had burned.

Deep Fried Shrimp Balls: A recent favorite at our go to dim sum restautrant, but these were small and chewy. Like everything else, it had little flavor, which I usually find shrimp a little overpowering, but I could barely even taste the shrimp, it was so bland.

Soy Sauce Bean Sprout Chow Mein: Something new, but not something we would order again. The noodles were dry and had little flavor other than a hint of soy sauce.

Stir Fry Mixed Vegetables: This was the item off the regular menu as we like to have vegetables with our meal. It consisted of carrot, bok choy (a pleasant surprise and one of my favorites), broccoli, a white broccoli looking thing, but it was not traditional cauliflower, snow peas, garlic, and celery. This was the warmest thing of them all, and it was still not quite hot. It was something we could make at home and definitely not worth $10. It was mostly celery, bok choy, broccoli, and miscellaneously sized garlic pieces.

Mango Pudding: Another staple in our group. It was set well, and very smooth, but the more we ate, we realized it tasted artificial. It was sweet, but in a sugary sweet, not a ripe mango sweet. It tasted like it was made with mango extract and overall was disappointing.

Steamed Custard Buns: The same bun recipe as the pan fried pork buns, not bad, but overall bland. The custard inside was vanilla, but it tasted extremely artificial. None of us really enjoyed it.<//review>

<Time>1572674105869</Time><Rating>3<//Rating>< review>
Tl;dr - decent food, authentic menu. Good menu variety. Slow service and a little pricey.

Some of the dishes were fantastic and some were poorly executed. The pig feet with peanuts was really nice and well cooked. The siu mai were delicious.

The bbq pork buns were definitely the worst I've ever seen. They looked mangled and the meat inside was not great.

The shrimp dumplings were average.

There were definitely some authentic menu items that I'm interested in trying. There are also some American-friendly options for those that aren't adventurous.

Service was a little slow but we weren't in a rush so it was ok.

Atmosphere was good. Feels like China.</review>

< review>
Absolutely the best brick and mortar reloading business in many of miles. I am fortunate its only 7 miles from my bench. Brian stocks just about everything you could want, and a lot that is hard to believe. Prices are a bit more than Midway(online). but less than Turners or Fowlers. If you  consider the shipping and the tactile instant gratification factor , than Midway loses. Other local shops just cant measure up in terms of stock and knowledge. There is some pretty obscure stuff here for us odd caliber knuckleheads, and lots of stuff that hasn't been made in decades. From mundane to exotic, good chance you'll find something to baste your barrels with. Plus a damn good conversation about the minutia that makes reloading  so fulfilling. Be thankful to have such a resource in your  backyard. I sure as hell am.
Aim to the left, that's where the enemy lies.<//review>

< text>
Support your local reloading supply store. The owner Brian is very knowledgeable and helped me get my reloading bench up and running. He will help guide you when it comes to basics and will go over everything with you to help you pick the right equipment for your bench.What I really like is that he doesn't try to upsell and he truly listens to what you want. He is very friendly and is always just a phone call away if you have a question about reloading. He definitely seems to have a passion for this and every time I come in to pick up supplies we have a good conversation. The store is well stocked with a wide variety of powders, primers, and bullets. He has everything you need. However if you need a large quantity of components, I would recommend you call him ahead of time and have him order it. It's a very far drive out to Anaheim for me and I like to stock up while I am there. It can be a little disappointing when I get there and there are only a few pounds of the powder I plan to use.< /text>

This was my first time at Larkspur Landing Optometry (now located in Corte Madera), and i am so happy that i was referred to this business. Because I visited during COVID, I have to say that the staff really went above and beyond to make sure all safety guidelines were met and exceeded and I never once felt threatened that I may be putting myself at risk by being seen there. < response>
{'time': 1576799275470, 'text': "It's hard to say that we have a lack of technology when we use the 'gold standard' of eye pressure measurement, which is known as Goldmann Applanation Tonometry. This includes using a drop of anesthetic and a non-toxic dye, then slightly touching the surface of your eye to accurately measure your eye pressure. The eye pressure is measured by the amount of force it takes to gently flatten a fixed area of the cornea. We also could've looked in the back of your eye more extensively, if we felt you needed it, using our other technology (OCT Scanner and Fundus Camera) but you would've been charged for it because it's a separate service on your insurance. Also, this service is not to be done in place of a dilation according to the rules of your insurance. Look at us go.... checking your eye health to the highest standard of care AND saving you money!\n\nBetween the staff on the floor, we have over 11 years of experience in ordering and dealing with different lens designs, treatments, etc. Our apologies as we were severely short staffed that day, one of our opticians happened to be off that day and our Practice Manager was on his way back from the ER during your appointment. <Review>I have been a recent physical therapy patient at Silver Creek Physical Therapy in San Jose after my two hip replacements.   My first experience was in January of 2019; and the second in January and February of 2021. I am currently 75 years old and previously had seen a variety of physical therapists over about a 15 year period for chronic low back and sciatica pain. <Review>I had an excellent experience at Silver Creek Physical Therapy, and I highly recommend them.  I was referred to them by my physician for treatment of pain caused by bursitis in my right hip.

My physical therapist Dr. Dominic Baiocco was very knowledgeable and skillful both in diagnosis and treatment.  He located the exact areas of the inflammation and tailored treatments and exercises to improve my strength and flexibility, which restored my ability to walk and work with much less pain.  He was very careful to coach me in the correct ways to do the exercises so that I would not only get the most advantage from them, but would also avoid causing myself more pain.  He also advised me how to go about daily activities in ways that would avoid making the bursitis worse.  His cheerful manner motivated me to keep coming back in order to achieve the maximum improvement.

The assisting staff were also very helpful.  They would lead me through the details of various exercises and help me with the equipment in order get the maximum benefit and avoid difficulties.  They were always so polite and kind that it made the experience a pleasant one.

The facility is clean and well organized.  The staff at the front desk were very courteous and helpful, and when some unexpected conflicts came up in my schedule they responded by promptly helping me find and book alternate dates and times.

I have happily recommended Silver Creek Physical Therapy to others, and they have also found them to be excellent.<//Review><Rating>5</Rating>< pics>

< Review>
Love the Rack but don't expect to go in and find your whole wardrobe in a single visit. To be successful shopping here you need to stop in regularly. Example, I've been looking for some shoes for hiking and the pair I was most interested in were Merrell. I had been online shopping quite a bit but just didn't want to pull the trigger. Stopped in one of my local Rack stores and low and behold they had a sweet pair of Merrells for $65, anywhere else $100. Went back a few days later they were all gone. The stores are usually organized by category (shorts, t-shirts, etc) and clearly marked by size. The pricing is always great and of course they offer the best brands. Highly recommend you stop in a Rack when you have a birthday present to buy for your significant other. Oh, and sign up for the Nordstrom debit card which is attached to your bank account (like Targets Red card) cuz you might as well gets points while your spending money.< /Review>
